# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

82-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed my investigation of the Kafka Streams topology build process and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary of Findings

I traced the complete flow of how a Kafka Streams topology is built and compiled to a processor node chain:

**Key Build Chain:**
1. **StreamsBuilder.build()** - Public API entry point that initiates the build process
2. **InternalStreamsBuilder.buildAndOptimizeTopology()** - Optimizes the topology graph
3. **InternalTopologyBuilder.buildTopology()** - Compiles the logical topology to a physical ProcessorTopology
4. **InternalTopologyBuilder.build()** - Creates ProcessorNode instances from NodeFactory objects and materializes StateStore objects
5. **StreamTask.initializeTopology()** - Initializes processor nodes at task execution time by calling node.init() on each ProcessorNode

**Key Components:**
- **InternalTopologyBuilder** - Contains node factories, state factories, and performs the actual compilation
- **ProcessorTopology** - Immutable physical topology containing processor nodes, source nodes, sink nodes, and state stores
- **StoreBuilder** - User-provided store definitions that are wrapped and materialized via StoreFactory during topology compilation
- **StreamTask** - Executes the ProcessorTopology with proper state management and context initialization

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, relevant symbols, the execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the entire process.

used to overwrite the\\n435:      * serdes in {@link Materialized}, i.e.,\\n436:      * <pre> {@code\\n437:      * streamBuilder.globalTable(topic, Consumed.with(Serde.String(), Serde.String()), Materialized.<String, String, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>as(storeName))\\n438:      * }\\n439:      * </pre>\\n440:      * To query the local {@link ReadOnlyKeyValueStore} it must be obtained {@link GlobalKTable} for the specified topic\\n458:      */\\n459:     public synchronized <K, V> GlobalKTable<K, V> globalTable(final String topic,\\n460:                                                               final Consumed<K, V> consumed,\\n461:                                                               final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\\n462: import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * {@code StreamsBuilder} provides the high-level Kafka Streams DSL to specify a Kafka Streams topology.\n51:  *\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * It is a This also means that the work\n188:      * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n189:      * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n190:      * <p>\n191:      * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n192:      * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n193:      * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n194:      *\n195:      * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n196:      * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n197:      */\n198:     public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n199:         return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     /**\n203:      * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n204:      * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n205:      * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n206:      * <p>\n207:      * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n208:      * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics.
